1. # Hazard Hero
2. 
3. Hazard Hero is a **one-sign pilot** for accessible parking assistance. The pilot proves one simple loop:
4. 
5. 1. A visitor waves at the installed sign.
6. 2. The sign sends a 512-sample reading to the backend.
7. 3. The backend marks the sign as `assistance_requested`.
8. 4. A staff member sees the request in the app, acknowledges it, and resolves it.
9. 5. The sign returns to `available`.
10. 
11. If that loop works reliably for one installed sign, the pilot is successful.
12. 
13. ## Pilot scope
14. 
15. ### In scope
16. 
17. - One installed ESP32 sign
18. - One backend environment
19. - One operator account or one small pilot team
20. - One mobile operator workflow
21. - One fixed installation location
22. - Basic event history for request, acknowledge, and resolve actions
23. 
24. ### Explicitly deferred
25. 
26. These items may exist elsewhere in the repo, but they are **not required for pilot launch**:
27. 
28. - Multi-org or fleet management workflows
29. - Rich site and parking-space administration
30. - Full QR/device claim operations for scaled deployment
31. - OTA update workflows
32. - Push notifications as a launch dependency
33. - Training-mode productization
34. - Old social/media/template features from earlier repo history
35. 
36. See `PILOT.md` for the detailed pilot definition and launch checklist.
37. 
38. ## Pilot architecture
39. 
40. ```text
41. ESP32 sign
42.   -> GET /api/v1/devices/{serial}/status
43.   -> when status == available, collect 512 ADC samples
44.   -> POST /api/v1/inference/classify
45.   -> backend changes sign to assistance_requested when a wave is detected
46.   -> staff app shows the request
47.   -> staff acknowledges and resolves the request
48. ```
49. 
50. Primary sign states for the pilot:
51. 
52. `available -> assistance_requested -> assistance_in_progress -> available`
53. 
54. ## Repository layout
55. 
56. ```text
57. smart-handicap-sign/
58. ├── backend/      FastAPI API, async services, embedded inference
59. ├── frontend/     React Native + Expo operator app
60. ├── database/     PostgreSQL schema and migration scripts
61. ├── firmware/     ESP-IDF firmware for the pilot sign
62. ├── hardware/     Legacy MicroPython implementation
63. ├── ai/           Model training code
64. └── PILOT.md      Pilot scope and launch checklist
65. ```
66. 
67. ## Quick start
68. 
69. ### Prerequisites
70. 
71. - Node.js 18+
72. - Python 3.12 for the backend
73. - Docker Desktop
74. - PostgreSQL access via `docker compose`
75. - WorkOS credentials for auth
76. 
77. ### Local setup
78. 
79. 1. Install workspace dependencies:
80. 
81.    ```bash
82.    npm install
83.    ```
84. 
85. 2. Configure environment variables:
86. 
87.    - `backend/.env`
88.    - `frontend/.env`
89. 
90. 3. Start Postgres:
91. 
92.    ```bash
93.    npm run db:up
94.    ```
95. 
96. 4. Apply the schema:
97. 
98.    ```bash
99.    npm run db:migrate
100.    ```
101. 
102. 5. Run the backend:
103. 
104.    ```bash
105.    cd backend
106.    pip install -r requirements.txt
107.    uvicorn app.main:app --host 0.0.0.0 --port 8000 --reload
108.    ```
109. 
110.    To open a live matplotlib graph for every inference payload during local debugging,
111.    set `INFERENCE_DEBUG_PLOT_ENABLED=true` in `backend/.env` before starting the backend.
112. 
113. 6. Run the frontend:
114. 
115.    ```bash
116.    cd frontend
117.    npm start
118.    ```
119. 
120. 7. Flash and provision the pilot sign using `firmware/README.md`.
121. 
122. ## Pilot operations
123. 
124. For the pilot, operators only need to:
125. 
126. 1. Log in.
127. 2. Watch the current sign status.
128. 3. Acknowledge a new assistance request.
129. 4. Resolve the request after helping the visitor.
130. 
131. Setup, manufacturing, and scale-out workflows should not be treated as launch blockers.
132. 
133. ## Key API endpoints for the pilot
134. 
135. - `GET /health`
136. - `GET /api/v1/status`
137. - `GET /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/status`
138. - `POST /api/v1/inference/classify`
139. - `POST /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/acknowledge`
140. - `POST /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/resolve`
141. 
142. ## Validation
143. 
144. Useful repo commands for the pilot:
145. 
146. ```bash
147. # Backend tests
148. cd backend
149. pytest
150. 
151. # Frontend lint
152. npm run lint --workspace=frontend
153. 
154. # Frontend tests (placeholder suite)
155. npm run test --workspace=frontend
156. ```
157. 
158. Firmware validation depends on an ESP-IDF 5.4+ environment; see `firmware/README.md` and `firmware/TEST_PLAN.md`.
159. 
160. ## Related docs
161. 
162. - `PILOT.md` - pilot definition and launch checklist
163. - `firmware/README.md` - flash, configure, and operate the pilot sign
164. - `firmware/TEST_PLAN.md` - hardware validation checklist for the pilot sign
165. - `WORKOS_SETUP.md` - auth provider setup
166. 
167. ## Status
168. 
169. This repository still contains some post-pilot or legacy building blocks. When documentation and implementation disagree, treat the **one-sign pilot flow** as the current product target.
170.

18. router = APIRouter(prefix="/inference", tags=["inference"])

21. SAMPLE_COUNT = SIGNAL_CONFIG["sample_count"]
22. MAX_ADC_VALUE = SIGNAL_CONFIG["max_value"]

25. class ClassifyRequest(BaseModel):
26.     serial_number: Optional[str] = Field(
27.         default=None,
28.         min_length=1,
29.         description="The serial number of the device submitting the signal",
30.     )
31.     samples: List[int] = Field(
32.         ...,
33.         min_length=SAMPLE_COUNT,
34.         max_length=SAMPLE_COUNT,
35.         description=f"Exactly {SAMPLE_COUNT} integers in the range 0-{MAX_ADC_VALUE} (ESP32 12-bit ADC)",
36.     )
37. 
38. 
39. class ClassifyResponse(BaseModel):
40.     label: str
41.     confidence: float
42. 
43. 
44. @lru_cache(maxsize=1)
45. def _get_classifier() -> WaveClassifier:
46.     logger.info("Loading wave-detection model …")
47.     clf = WaveClassifier()
48.     logger.info("Wave-detection model loaded successfully")
49.     return clf
50. 
51. 
52. @router.post("/classify", response_model=ClassifyResponse)
53. async def classify(
54.     payload: ClassifyRequest,
55.     device: AuthenticatedDevice = Depends(get_authenticated_device),
56. ):
57.     await device_service.update_device_last_seen(device.serial_number)
58. 
59.     if payload.serial_number and payload.serial_number != device.serial_number:
60.         return JSONResponse(
61.             status_code=403,
62.             content={"error": "Device can only submit telemetry for its own serial number"},
63.         )
64.     if not payload.serial_number:
65.         payload.serial_number = device.serial_number
66. 
67.     clf = _get_classifier()
68. 
69.     try:
70.         result = clf.classify(payload.samples, threshold=WAVE_THRESHOLD)
71.     except ValueError as exc:
72.         return JSONResponse(
73.             status_code=422,
74.             content={"error": "Validation Error", "message": str(exc)},
75.         )
76. 
77.     logger.info(
78.         "Inference — device=%s label=%s confidence=%.4f",
79.         device.serial_number,
80.         result["label"],
81.         result["confidence"],
82.     )
83. 
84.     settings = get_settings()
85.     if settings.inference_debug_plot_enabled:
86.         render_signal_debug_plot(
87.             payload.samples,
88.             serial_number=payload.serial_number,
89.             label=result["label"],
90.             confidence=result["confidence"],
91.         )
92. 
93.     if result["label"] == "wave" and payload.serial_number:
94.         try:
95.             transition = await device_service.transition_device_status(
96.                 serial_number=payload.serial_number,
97.                 expected_status="available",
98.                 new_status="assistance_requested",
99.                 event_type="assistance_requested",
100.                 payload={"confidence": result["confidence"]},
101.             )
102.             if transition.success:
103.                 logger.info("Device %s set to assistance_requested", payload.serial_number)
104.             elif transition.error_code != "invalid_status_transition":
105.                 logger.warning(
106.                     "Wave detected for %s but status update failed with %s",
107.                     payload.serial_number,
108.                     transition.error_code,
109.                 )
110.         except Exception:
111.             logger.exception("Failed to update device state for %s", payload.serial_number)
112. 
113.     return result
114.

137.     _current_user: CurrentUser = Depends(get_current_user),
138. ):

140.         device = await _get_device_or_404(serial_number)

11. @dataclass
12. class DeviceTransitionResult:
13.     success: bool
14.     device: Optional[dict] = None
15.     error_code: Optional[str] = None
16.     current_status: Optional[str] = None
17. 
18. 
19. _DEVICE_COLUMNS = """
20.     id,
21.     serial_number,
22.     model_code,
23.     hardware_revision,
24.     firmware_version,
25.     operational_status,
26.     last_seen_at,
27.     name,
28.     created_at,
29.     updated_at
30. """
31. 
32. 
33. def _row_to_dict(row) -> dict:
34.     device = dict(row)
35.     if device.get("id"):
36.         device["id"] = str(device["id"])
37.     device.setdefault("lifecycle_status", "active")
38.     device.setdefault("claim_status", None)
39.     device.setdefault("organization_id", None)
40.     device.setdefault("current_site_id", None)
41.     device.setdefault("current_parking_space_id", None)
42.     return device
43. 
44. 
45. def _normalize_event_payload(payload: Any) -> dict[str, Any]:
46.     if isinstance(payload, dict):
47.         return payload
48.     if isinstance(payload, str):
49.         try:
50.             decoded = json.loads(payload)
51.         except json.JSONDecodeError:
52.             return {"raw": payload}
53.         return decoded if isinstance(decoded, dict) else {"value": decoded}
54.     if payload is None:
55.         return {}
56.     return {"value": payload}
57. 
58. 
59. def _event_row_to_dict(row) -> dict:
60.     event = dict(row)
61.     event["id"] = str(event["id"])
62.     event["device_id"] = str(event["device_id"])
63.     event["payload"] = _normalize_event_payload(event.get("payload"))
64.     return event
65. 
66. 
67. async def get_device_by_serial(serial_number: str) -> Optional[dict]:
68.     pool = await get_pool()
69.     row = await pool.fetchrow(
70.         f"SELECT {_DEVICE_COLUMNS} FROM devices WHERE serial_number = $1",
71.         serial_number,
72.     )
73.     return _row_to_dict(row) if row else None
74. 
75. 
76. async def list_devices(*, skip: int = 0, limit: int = 100) -> list[dict]:
77.     pool = await get_pool()
78.     rows = await pool.fetch(
79.         f"""
80.         SELECT {_DEVICE_COLUMNS}
81.         FROM devices
82.         ORDER BY created_at ASC
83.         OFFSET $1 LIMIT $2
84.         """,
85.         skip,
86.         limit,
87.     )
88.     return [_row_to_dict(row) for row in rows]
89. 
90. 
91. async def update_device_last_seen(
92.     serial_number: str,
93.     *,
94.     seen_at: Optional[datetime] = None,
95. ) -> Optional[dict]:
96.     pool = await get_pool()
97.     timestamp = seen_at or datetime.now(timezone.utc)
98.     row = await pool.fetchrow(
99.         f"""
100.         UPDATE devices
101.         SET last_seen_at = $2,
102.             updated_at = NOW()
103.         WHERE serial_number = $1
104.         RETURNING {_DEVICE_COLUMNS}
105.         """,
106.         serial_number,
107.         timestamp,
108.     )
109.     return _row_to_dict(row) if row else None
110. 
111. 
112. async def transition_device_status(
113.     *,
114.     serial_number: str,
115.     expected_status: str,
116.     new_status: str,
117.     event_type: str,
118.     actor_user_id: Optional[str] = None,
119.     payload: Optional[dict[str, Any]] = None,
120. ) -> DeviceTransitionResult:
121.     pool = await get_pool()
122. 
123.     async with pool.acquire() as conn:
124.         async with conn.transaction():
125.             current = await conn.fetchrow(
126.                 f"SELECT {_DEVICE_COLUMNS} FROM devices WHERE serial_number = $1 FOR UPDATE",
127.                 serial_number,
128.             )
129.             if current is None:
130.                 return DeviceTransitionResult(success=False, error_code="device_not_found")
131. 
132.             current_device = _row_to_dict(current)
133.             current_status = current_device["operational_status"]
134.             if current_status != expected_status:
135.                 return DeviceTransitionResult(
136.                     success=False,
137.                     error_code="invalid_status_transition",
138.                     device=current_device,
139.                     current_status=current_status,
140.                 )
141. 
142.             updated = await conn.fetchrow(
143.                 f"""
144.                 UPDATE devices
145.                 SET operational_status = $2,
146.                     updated_at = NOW()
147.                 WHERE serial_number = $1
148.                 RETURNING {_DEVICE_COLUMNS}
149.                 """,
150.                 serial_number,
151.                 new_status,
152.             )
153. 
154.             event_payload = {
155.                 "previous_status": expected_status,
156.                 "new_status": new_status,
157.             }
158.             if actor_user_id:
159.                 event_payload["actor_user_id"] = actor_user_id
160.             if payload:
161.                 event_payload.update(payload)
162. 
163.             await conn.execute(
164.                 """
165.                 INSERT INTO device_events (device_id, event_type, payload)
166.                 VALUES ($1::uuid, $2, $3::jsonb)
167.                 """,
168.                 str(updated["id"]),
169.                 event_type,
170.                 json.dumps(event_payload),
171.             )
172. 
173.     return DeviceTransitionResult(success=True, device=_row_to_dict(updated))
174. 
175. 
176. async def create_device_event(
177.     *,
178.     serial_number: str,
179.     event_type: str,
180.     payload: Optional[dict[str, Any]] = None,
181. ) -> Optional[dict]:
182.     pool = await get_pool()
183.     row = await pool.fetchrow(
184.         """
185.         INSERT INTO device_events (device_id, event_type, payload)
186.         SELECT id, $2, $3::jsonb
187.         FROM devices
188.         WHERE serial_number = $1
189.         RETURNING id, device_id, event_type, payload, created_at
190.         """,
191.         serial_number,
192.         event_type,
193.         json.dumps(payload or {}),
194.     )
195.     if row is None:
196.         return None
197.     return _event_row_to_dict(row)
198. 
199. 
200. async def get_device_events(*, serial_number: str, skip: int = 0, limit: int = 50) -> list[dict]:
201.     pool = await get_pool()
202.     rows = await pool.fetch(
203.         """
204.         SELECT de.id, de.device_id, de.event_type, de.payload, de.created_at
205.         FROM device_events de
206.         JOIN devices d ON d.id = de.device_id
207.         WHERE d.serial_number = $1
208.         ORDER BY de.created_at DESC
209.         OFFSET $2 LIMIT $3
210.         """,
211.         serial_number,
212.         skip,
213.         limit,
214.     )
215. 
216.     results = []
217.     for row in rows:
218.         results.append(_event_row_to_dict(row))
219.     return results

C:\Users\KBishop\code\apps\smart-handicap-sign\database\README.md (lines 1-220)
1. # Database
2. 
3. PostgreSQL 15 schema assets for the one-sign Hazard Hero pilot.
4. 
5. ## Canonical assets
6. 
7. - `schemas/shs_schema.sql` — bootstrap entrypoint used by Docker and local setup
8. - `schemas/shs_schema_v2.sql` — canonical pilot schema loaded by `shs_schema.sql`
9. - `seeds/dev_data_v2.sql` — deterministic pilot sign bootstrap data
10. - `scripts/migrate_v2.ts` — default migration entrypoint
11. 
12. ## Commands
13. 
14. Run these from `database/`:
15. 
16. ```bash
17. npm run migrate
18. npm run migrate:last-seen
19. npm run load:sign
20. npm run seed
21. ```
22. 
23. The scripts load `../backend/.env` and expect `POSTGRES_CONNECTION_STRING` (or `DATABASE_URL` for the sign load script) to point at the target PostgreSQL instance.
24. 
25. ## Migration behavior
26. 
27. `npm run migrate` drops and recreates the database as the pilot schema. It is destructive by design and should only be used where data reset is acceptable.
28. 
29. `npm run migrate:last-seen` is an additive migration that only ensures `devices.last_seen_at` exists on an already-provisioned pilot database.
30. 
31. ## Pilot schema overview
32. 
33. The pilot database keeps only the tables needed for a single operator + single sign workflow:
34. 
35. - `users`
36. - `profiles`
37. - `devices`
38. - `device_events`
39. 
40. ## Device states
41. 
42. `device_operational_status` supports only the pilot loop and basic health states:
43. 
44. - `available`
45. - `assistance_requested`
46. - `assistance_in_progress`
47. - `offline`
48. - `error`
49. 
50. Training states, organization tables, installation/claim workflow tables, push tokens, notifications, and billing/subscription fields are intentionally removed from the canonical schema.
51. 
52. ## Pilot sign bootstrap
53. 
54. `npm run load:sign` applies `seeds/dev_data_v2.sql`, which creates only the pilot sign/device row required by the runtime API. It does not create user, profile, organization, parking-space, or device-event records.
55. 
56. `npm run seed` is kept as a backwards-compatible alias for the same sign-only load.
57. 
58. The seeded device token is `pilot-device-token` with serial `SHS-2605-S01-A7K-00001-J` for local pilot testing.
59.

26. export function createApiServices(apiClient: ApiClient) {
27.   const authAPI = {
28.     initiateLogin: async (redirectUri?: string): Promise<LoginInitResponse> => {
29.       const params = redirectUri ? `?redirect_uri=${encodeURIComponent(redirectUri)}` : "";
30.       return apiClient.get<LoginInitResponse>(`/auth/login${params}`);
31.     },
32.     handleCallback: async (code: string): Promise<AuthResponse> => {
33.       return apiClient.post<AuthResponse>("/auth/exchange", { data: { code } });
34.     },
35.     getCurrentUser: async (): Promise<User> => {
36.       const response = await apiClient.get<{ user: User }>("/auth/me");
37.       return response.user;
38.     },
39.     initiateLogout: async (): Promise<initiateLogoutResponse> => {
40.       return apiClient.post<initiateLogoutResponse>("/auth/logout");
41.     },
42.   };
43. 
44.   const organizationAPI = {
45.     getOrganizations: async (): Promise<Organization[]> => {
46.       return apiClient.get<Organization[]>("/organizations");
47.     },
48.     getOrganization: async (orgId: string): Promise<Organization> => {
49.       return apiClient.get<Organization>(`/organizations/${orgId}`);
50.     },
51.     createOrganization: async (name: string): Promise<Organization> => {
52.       return apiClient.post<Organization>("/organizations", { name });
53.     },
54.     updateOrganization: async (orgId: string, name: string): Promise<Organization> => {
55.       return apiClient.patch<Organization>(`/organizations/${orgId}`, { name });
56.     },
57.     deleteOrganization: async (orgId: string): Promise<void> => {
58.       await apiClient.delete<void>(`/organizations/${orgId}`);
59.     },
60.     getMembers: async (orgId: string): Promise<OrgMember[]> => {
61.       return apiClient.get<OrgMember[]>(`/organizations/${orgId}/members`);
62.     },
63.     addMember: async (orgId: string, email: string, role: OrgRole = "member"): Promise<OrgMember> => {
64.       return apiClient.post<OrgMember>(`/organizations/${orgId}/members`, { email, role });
65.     },
66.     updateMemberRole: async (orgId: string, userId: string, role: OrgRole): Promise<OrgMember> => {
67.       return apiClient.patch<OrgMember>(`/organizations/${orgId}/members/${userId}`, { role });
68.     },
69.     removeMember: async (orgId: string, userId: string): Promise<void> => {
70.       await apiClient.delete<void>(`/organizations/${orgId}/members/${userId}`);
71.     },
72.   };

74.   const notificationAPI = {
75.     getNotifications: async (

78.     ): Promise<SignNotification[]> => {

81.       if (params?.read !== undefined) query.append("read", String(params.read));
82.       const qs = query.toString();
83.       return apiClient.get<SignNotification[]>(`/notifications${qs ? `?${qs}` : ""}`, config);
84.     },

102. 
103.   const devicesAPI = {
104.     list: async (
105.       params?: { organization_id?: string; lifecycle_status?: DeviceLifecycleStatus },
106.       config?: unknown,
107.     ): Promise<Device[]> => {
108.       const query = new URLSearchParams();
109.       if (params?.organization_id) query.append("organization_id", params.organization_id);
110.       if (params?.lifecycle_status) query.append("lifecycle_status", params.lifecycle_status);
111.       const qs = query.toString();
112.       return apiClient.get<Device[]>(`/devices${qs ? `?${qs}` : ""}`, config);
113.     },
114.     getBySerial: async (serialNumber: string): Promise<Device> => {
115.       return apiClient.get<Device>(`/devices/${encodeURIComponent(serialNumber)}`);
116.     },
117.     acknowledge: async (serialNumber: string): Promise<Device> => {
118.       return apiClient.post<Device>(`/devices/${encodeURIComponent(serialNumber)}/acknowledge`);
119.     },
120.     resolve: async (serialNumber: string): Promise<Device> => {
121.       return apiClient.post<Device>(`/devices/${encodeURIComponent(serialNumber)}/resolve`);
122.     },
123.     revoke: async (serialNumber: string, request: RevokeRequest): Promise<Device> => {
124.       return apiClient.post<Device>(`/devices/${encodeURIComponent(serialNumber)}/revoke`, request);
125.     },
126.     transfer: async (serialNumber: string, request: TransferRequest): Promise<Device> => {
127.       return apiClient.post<Device>(`/devices/${encodeURIComponent(serialNumber)}/transfer`, request);
128.     },
129.     release: async (serialNumber: string): Promise<Device> => {
130.       return apiClient.post<Device>(`/devices/${encodeURIComponent(serialNumber)}/release`);
131.     },
132.     regenerateClaim: async (serialNumber: string): Promise<{ claim_id: string }> => {
133.       return apiClient.post<{ claim_id: string }>(`/devices/${encodeURIComponent(serialNumber)}/regenerate-claim`);
134.     },
135.     getEvents: async (serialNumber: string, config?: unknown): Promise<DeviceEvent[]> => {
136.       return apiClient.get<DeviceEvent[]>(`/devices/${encodeURIComponent(serialNumber)}/events`, config);
137.     },
138.   };
139. 
140.   const deviceClaimsAPI = {
141.     validate: async (request: ClaimValidateRequest): Promise<ClaimValidateResponse> => {
142.       return apiClient.post<ClaimValidateResponse>("/device-claims/validate", request);
143.     },
144.     claim: async (request: ClaimRequest): Promise<ClaimResponse> => {
145.       return apiClient.post<ClaimResponse>("/device-claims/claim", request);
146.     },
147.   };
148. 
149.   const sitesAPI = {
150.     list: async (organizationId?: string): Promise<Site[]> => {
151.       const query = organizationId ? `?organization_id=${organizationId}` : "";
152.       return apiClient.get<Site[]>(`/sites${query}`);
153.     },
154.     get: async (siteId: string): Promise<Site> => {
155.       return apiClient.get<Site>(`/sites/${siteId}`);
156.     },
157.     create: async (site: SiteCreate): Promise<Site> => {
158.       return apiClient.post<Site>("/sites", site);
159.     },
160.     update: async (siteId: string, updates: Partial<SiteCreate>): Promise<Site> => {
161.       return apiClient.patch<Site>(`/sites/${siteId}`, updates);
162.     },
163.     delete: async (siteId: string): Promise<void> => {
164.       await apiClient.delete<void>(`/sites/${siteId}`);
165.     },
166.     listParkingSpaces: async (siteId: string): Promise<ParkingSpace[]> => {
167.       return apiClient.get<ParkingSpace[]>(`/sites/${siteId}/parking-spaces`);
168.     },
169.     createParkingSpace: async (siteId: string, space: Omit<ParkingSpaceCreate, "site_id">): Promise<ParkingSpace> => {
170.       return apiClient.post<ParkingSpace>(`/sites/${siteId}/parking-spaces`, space);
171.     },
172.     getParkingSpace: async (spaceId: string): Promise<ParkingSpace> => {
173.       return apiClient.get<ParkingSpace>(`/parking-spaces/${spaceId}`);
174.     },
175.     updateParkingSpace: async (spaceId: string, updates: Partial<ParkingSpaceCreate>): Promise<ParkingSpace> => {
176.       return apiClient.patch<ParkingSpace>(`/parking-spaces/${spaceId}`, updates);
177.     },
178.     deleteParkingSpace: async (spaceId: string): Promise<void> => {
179.       await apiClient.delete<void>(`/parking-spaces/${spaceId}`);
180.     },
181.   };

184.     authAPI,
185.     organizationAPI,
186.     notificationAPI,
187.     pushTokenAPI,
188.     devicesAPI,
189.     deviceClaimsAPI,
190.     sitesAPI,
191.   };

28. function formatRelativeTime(iso: string): string {
29.     const diff = Date.now() - new Date(iso).getTime();
30.     const minutes = Math.floor(diff / 60_000);
31.     if (minutes < 1) return 'Just now';
32.     if (minutes < 60) return `${minutes}m ago`;
33.     const hours = Math.floor(minutes / 60);
34.     if (hours < 24) return `${hours}h ago`;
35.     return `${Math.floor(hours / 24)}d ago`;
36. }
37. 
38. function formatLastSeen(iso: string | null): string {
39.     if (!iso) {
40.         return 'Last seen never';
41.     }
42. 
43.     const date = new Date(iso);
44.     if (Number.isNaN(date.getTime())) {
45.         return 'Last seen unknown';
46.     }
47. 
48.     return `Last seen ${date.toLocaleString()} (${formatRelativeTime(iso)})`;
49. }

11. function formatDate(iso: string): string {
12.     const d = new Date(iso);
13.     return d.toLocaleDateString(undefined, {
14.         weekday: 'long',
15.         year: 'numeric',
16.         month: 'long',
17.         day: 'numeric',
18.     }) + ' at ' + d.toLocaleTimeString(undefined, {
19.         hour: 'numeric',
20.         minute: '2-digit',
21.     });
22. }

24. function formatEventTitle(event: DeviceEvent): string {
25.     switch (event.event_type) {
26.         case 'assistance_requested':
27.             return 'Assistance requested';
28.         case 'assistance_acknowledged':
29.             return 'Request acknowledged';
30.         case 'assistance_resolved':
31.             return 'Request resolved';
32.         case 'pilot_seeded':
33.             return 'Pilot sign created';
34.         default:
35.             return event.event_type.replace(/_/g, ' ');
36.     }
37. }
38. 
39. function formatEventBody(event: DeviceEvent): string {
40.     const message = typeof event.payload?.message === 'string' ? event.payload.message : null;
41.     if (message) return message;
42. 
43.     const previousStatus = typeof event.payload?.previous_status === 'string'
44.         ? event.payload.previous_status
45.         : null;
46.     const newStatus = typeof event.payload?.new_status === 'string'
47.         ? event.payload.new_status
48.         : null;
49.     const confidence = typeof event.payload?.confidence === 'number'
50.         ? `${Math.round(event.payload.confidence * 100)}% confidence`
51.         : null;
52. 
53.     const parts = [
54.         previousStatus && newStatus ? `${previousStatus} -> ${newStatus}` : newStatus,
55.         confidence,
56.     ].filter(Boolean);
57. 
58.     if (parts.length > 0) {

1. import type { Device, DeviceLifecycleStatus } from '../types/device';
2. import { colors } from '../theme/colors';
3. 
4. type EnvReader = {
5.     process?: {
6.         env?: Record<string, string | undefined>;
7.     };
8. };
9. 
10. const DEFAULT_STALE_THRESHOLD_MINUTES = 15;
11. const STALE_THRESHOLD_ENV_KEY = 'EXPO_PUBLIC_DEVICE_STALE_MINUTES';
12. 
13. const LIFECYCLE_STATUS: Record<DeviceLifecycleStatus, { label: string; color: string }> = {
14.     active: { label: 'Ready for requests', color: '#34C759' },
15.     manufactured: { label: 'Not active yet', color: colors.textMuted },
16.     unclaimed: { label: 'Not active yet', color: colors.textMuted },
17.     claiming: { label: 'Setup in progress', color: colors.warning },
18.     lost: { label: 'Needs support', color: colors.negative },
19.     revoked: { label: 'Needs support', color: colors.negative },
20.     retired: { label: 'Offline', color: colors.textMuted },
21. };
22. 
23. const OPERATIONAL_STATUS: Record<string, { label: string; color: string; tone: string }> = {
24.     available: { label: 'Available', color: '#34C759', tone: '#34C75912' },
25.     assistance_requested: { label: 'Assistance Requested', color: colors.negative, tone: '#FF3B3012' },
26.     assistance_in_progress: { label: 'Assistance In Progress', color: colors.warning, tone: '#FF950012' },
27.     offline: { label: 'Offline', color: colors.textMuted, tone: '#86868B12' },
28.     error: { label: 'Needs Attention', color: colors.warning, tone: '#FF950012' },
29. };
30. 
31. function getConfiguredStaleThresholdMinutes(): number {
32.     const rawValue = (globalThis as typeof globalThis & EnvReader).process?.env?.[STALE_THRESHOLD_ENV_KEY]?.trim();
33.     if (!rawValue) {
34.         return DEFAULT_STALE_THRESHOLD_MINUTES;
35.     }
36. 
37.     const parsedMinutes = Number(rawValue);
38.     if (!Number.isFinite(parsedMinutes) || parsedMinutes <= 0) {
39.         return DEFAULT_STALE_THRESHOLD_MINUTES;
40.     }
41. 
42.     return parsedMinutes;
43. }
44. 
45. export function isDeviceStale(device: Device, now = new Date()): boolean {
46.     if (!device.last_seen_at) {
47.         return true;
48.     }
49. 
50.     const lastSeenMs = new Date(device.last_seen_at).getTime();
51.     if (Number.isNaN(lastSeenMs)) {
52.         return true;
53.     }
54. 
55.     return now.getTime() - lastSeenMs > getConfiguredStaleThresholdMinutes() * 60 * 1000;
56. }
57. 
58. export function getPilotStatus(device: Device, now = new Date()) {
59.     if (isDeviceStale(device, now)) {
60.         return OPERATIONAL_STATUS.offline;
61.     }
62. 
63.     if (device.lifecycle_status === 'active' && device.operational_status) {
64.         return OPERATIONAL_STATUS[device.operational_status] ?? OPERATIONAL_STATUS.available;
65.     }
66. 
67.     return {
68.         ...LIFECYCLE_STATUS[device.lifecycle_status],
69.         tone: `${LIFECYCLE_STATUS[device.lifecycle_status].color}12`,
70.     };
71. }

C:\Users\KBishop\code\apps\smart-handicap-sign\PILOT.md (lines 1-140)
1. # Hazard Hero Pilot Plan
2. 
3. ## Pilot definition
4. 
5. This pilot is a **single-sign, single-site proof of concept**. The goal is to prove one real-world outcome:
6. 
7. 1. A visitor triggers a help request at the sign.
8. 2. The backend records the request and changes the sign status.
9. 3. A staff member sees the request quickly.
10. 4. Staff acknowledges the request.
11. 5. Staff resolves the request and the sign returns to available.
12. 
13. If that loop works reliably with one installed sign, the pilot is successful.
14. 
15. ## What the pilot should include
16. 
17. ### Core scope
18. 
19. - **One physical sign**
20. - **One backend environment**
21. - **One organization or one shared operator account**
22. - **One staff-facing mobile app flow**
23. - **One notification path**: app polling is acceptable; push notifications are optional
24. - **One install location**
25. - **Basic event history** for requests, acknowledgements, and resolutions
26. 
27. ### Required states
28. 
29. - `available`
30. - `assistance_requested`
31. - `assistance_in_progress`
32. - `offline`
33. - return to `available`
34. 
35. For pilot purposes, `offline` should mean the sign has missed its expected backend check-ins long enough that staff should not trust the displayed availability until the device reconnects.
36. 
37. ### Required working surfaces in this repo
38. 
39. - **Firmware/device loop**
40.   - Poll sign status
41.   - Sample and send wave data
42.   - Respect backend status before classifying
43. - **Backend**
44.   - `POST /api/v1/inference/classify`
45.   - `GET /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/status`
46.   - `POST /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/acknowledge`
47.   - `POST /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/resolve`
48.   - device event logging
49. - **Frontend**
50.   - Login
51.   - Home screen showing current sign status
52.   - Acknowledge action
53.   - Resolve action
54.   - Basic request/event visibility
55. 
56. ## What should be removed from pilot scope
57. 
58. These items may remain in the repo, but they should be treated as **out of scope for pilot launch** and not block pilot completion.
59. 
60. ### Defer from launch
61. 
62. - Multi-organization administration
63. - Full member management and role complexity beyond what one pilot operator needs
64. - Full QR claim/install workflow
65. - Site and parking-space management UI beyond one seeded assignment
66. - Device fleet management for many devices
67. - Transfer / revoke / release workflows for pilot operations
68. - Claim ID regeneration workflows
69. - Push-token registration as a launch dependency
70. - Inference debug screens as part of the operator workflow
71. - OTA update workflows as a launch dependency
72. - Advanced firmware provisioning flows unless needed for this one install
73. - Training states:
74.   - `training_ready`
75.   - `training_positive`
76.   - `training_negative`
77. - Billing / subscription concepts
78. - Any old social/media/template leftovers in documentation
79. 
80. ### Recommended repo-level simplifications for pilot focus
81. 
82. - **Hide or ignore** non-pilot screens from normal navigation if they distract from the operator flow.
83. - **Seed one known device** and one known user instead of requiring the full installer claim process.
84. - **Treat sites / parking spaces as fixed setup data** for the pilot, not operator-managed content.
85. - **Use polling first**; add push later only if polling is too slow.
86. - **Make the home screen the primary pilot surface** and avoid requiring operators to visit secondary admin screens.
87. 
88. ## What may need to be added or tightened before pilot launch
89. 
90. ### Product and UX
91. 
92. - A clearly named **pilot operator flow**:
93.   - see current sign status
94.   - see new request
95.   - acknowledge
96.   - resolve
97. - Clear copy for each status so staff can act without training
98. - A visible last-updated or last-seen timestamp for device freshness
99. - A simple error/offline indicator for the sign
100. 
101. ### Backend
102. 
103. - Confirm `assistance_requested -> assistance_in_progress -> available` is the only supported operator loop for pilot
104. - Define the freshness rule that moves a sign into `offline`
105. - Ensure acknowledge and resolve actions create auditable device events
106. - Ensure one wave does not create noisy duplicate requests while already in a requested/in-progress state
107. - Ensure device status polling remains lightweight and stable
108. - Ensure the pilot can run with seeded data and minimal setup steps
109. 
110. ### Frontend
111. 
112. - Make the home screen robust when exactly one device is present
113. - Show the most recent request clearly
114. - Show `offline` as a distinct state, not as generic failure text
115. - Prevent double taps on acknowledge / resolve actions
116. - Show actionable failure states if the backend call fails
117. - Keep navigation minimal for pilot users
118. 
119. ### Firmware / device setup
120. 
121. - Lock in the production-like URL and credentials for the pilot device
122. - Verify the sign behaves safely when backend is unreachable
123. - Verify LED/status behavior matches the backend state machine
124. - Verify the sign does not continuously spam classify requests when unavailable
125. 
126. ### Documentation and ops
127. 
128. - Update repo-facing docs so the pilot story is obvious
129. - Document exact install steps for the one pilot sign
130. - Document operator steps for handling a request
131. - Document recovery steps for:
132.   - sign offline
133.   - backend unavailable
134.   - sign stuck in requested/in-progress state
135. 
136. ## Pilot launch checklist
137. 
138. ### Scope freeze
139. 
140. - [ ] Pilot success criteria are limited to one-sign end-to-end assistance handling

35. 7. Initialize ADC sampler
36. 8. Initialize HTTPS client
37. 9. Enter the main loop
38. 
39. Main loop:
40. 
41. - Poll `GET /devices/{serial}/status`
42. - Update the LED to match backend status
43. - If status is not `available`, wait 3 seconds and poll again
44. - If status is `available`, collect 200 samples over about 4.0 seconds
45. - Send the sample batch to `POST /inference/classify`
46. 
47. ## Supported sign states
48. 
49. The pilot relies on these core operational states:
50. 
51. - `available`
52. - `assistance_requested`
53. - `assistance_in_progress`
54. - `offline`
55. - `error`
56. 
57. ## Hardware assumptions
58. 
59. - ESP32-WROOM-32 class board
60. - 4 MB flash
61. - Photoresistor on **GPIO 34**
62. - Status LED on **GPIO 2**

279. ## Pilot operations checklist
280. 
281. Before installing the pilot sign:
282. 
283. 1. Set the backend URL.
284. 2. Replace `server_certs/ca_cert.pem` with the CA needed for the pilot backend.
285. 3. Flash the firmware.
286. 4. Manually preload serial number, auth token, and Wi-Fi credentials.
287. 5. Verify the sign can poll status.
288. 6. Verify a real wave triggers `assistance_requested`.
289. 7. Verify the operator can acknowledge and resolve the request.
290. 
291. ## Troubleshooting
292. 
293. ### Device boots into AP mode
294. 
295. - Wi-Fi credentials are missing
296. - Saved credentials are wrong
297. - The sign failed to reconnect too many times
298. 
299. ### Status polling fails
300. 
301. - Backend URL is wrong
302. - TLS certificate does not match the backend chain
303. - Device serial number or auth token is missing/invalid
304. - Backend is unavailable
305. 
306. ### Classification never runs
307. 
308. - Backend status is not `available`
309. - ADC wiring is wrong
310. - HTTPS client cannot reach `/inference/classify`

"*** Begin Patch\n*** Add File: C:\\Users\\KBishop\\.copilot\\session-state\\f991aa83-a4fc-40b6-9eaa-ef50b1fb8920\\plan.md\n+# Implementation Plan: Sign Offline / Assistance Notifications\n+\n+## Problem\n+\n+Add operator notifications when a sign goes `offline` or enters `assistance_requested`, without breaking the current one-sign pilot flow.\n+\n+## Current State Summary\n+\n+- **Backend runtime is pilot-only.** `backend/app/main.py` mounts only auth, inference, and device routes. Notification and push-token endpoints are currently absent, and `backend/tests/test_removed_routes.py` asserts `/api/v1/notifications` and `/api/v1/push-tokens` return 404.\n+- **Assistance requests already exist as device events.** `backend/app/routes/inference.py` changes a device from `available` to `assistance_requested` and records a `device_events` row via `device_service.transition_device_status(...)`.\n+- **Offline is only a frontend interpretation today.** The backend updates `devices.last_seen_at`, but it never transitions a device to `offline` or emits an offline event. `frontend_new/apps/mobile/src/screens/pilotStatus.ts` derives `offline` locally when `last_seen_at` is stale for 15 minutes.\n+- **Canonical pilot schema removed notification storage.** `database/schemas/shs_schema_v2.sql` drops `notifications` and `push_tokens`, and `database/README.md` says they are intentionally removed from the pilot schema.\n+- **Frontend has partial notification-era leftovers.** Shared API/types still define `notificationAPI`, `pushTokenAPI`, and `SignNotification`, but the mobile app currently uses device polling plus a `NotificationDetailScreen` for viewing a `DeviceEvent`, not an inbox. `expo-notifications` appears in `package-lock.json` but is not declared in `apps/mobile/package.json`.\n+\n+## Recommended Direction\n+\n+Build this in two layers so the pilot can ship incrementally:\n+\n+1. **Backend-authored notification records** for `assistance_requested` and `offline`, with deduplication and read state.\n+2. **Mobile consumption path** that can start as an in-app inbox/polling experience, with **Expo push delivery added only if required**.\n+\n+This keeps the first vertical slice aligned with the pilot guidance in `PILOT.md`, which explicitly allows polling as the notification path.\n+\n+## Architecture Decisions\n+\n+- **Treat notifications as a backend concern.** The backend should decide when a notification-worthy event occurs and persist a notification record instead of asking the mobile app to infer it.\n+- **Move offline detection server-side.** A real offline notification requires a server-side stale-device evaluator because the current frontend-only stale logic cannot notify a user who is not actively looking at the app.\n+- **Reuse device events as the source of truth.** Notification generation should hang off device status transitions / stale detection so the system has one auditable event stream.\n+- **Keep push optional.** Implement the persistence + API contract first; make Expo push an add-on delivery path.\n+\n+## Task List\n+\n+### Phase 1: Define the contract and data model\n+\n+#### Task 1: Finalize notification scope and delivery semantics\n+\n+**Description:** Decide the operator experience and backend rules before coding: notification channels, recipients, offline threshold, duplicate suppression, and how notifications relate to the existing pilot event history.\n+\n+**Acceptance criteria:**\n+- A single source of truth exists for which events create notifications (`assistance_requested`, `offline`).\n+- The plan defines the recipient model for pilot users.\n+- The plan defines whether the first implementation is inbox-only, push-enabled, or both.\n+\n+**Verification:**\n+- Open questions are resolved and 1. # Implementation Plan: Sign Offline / Assistance Notifications
2. 
3. ## Problem
4. 
5. Add operator notifications when a sign goes `offline` or enters `assistance_requested`, without breaking the current one-sign pilot flow.
6. 
7. ## Current State Summary
8. 
9. - **Backend runtime is pilot-only.** `backend/app/main.py` mounts only auth, inference, and device routes. Notification and push-token endpoints are currently absent, and `backend/tests/test_removed_routes.py` asserts `/api/v1/notifications` and `/api/v1/push-tokens` return 404.
10. - **Assistance requests already exist as device events.** `backend/app/routes/inference.py` changes a device from `available` to `assistance_requested` and records a `device_events` row via `device_service.transition_device_status(...)`.
11. - **Offline is only a frontend interpretation today.** The backend updates `devices.last_seen_at`, but it never transitions a device to `offline` or emits an offline event. `frontend_new/apps/mobile/src/screens/pilotStatus.ts` derives `offline` locally when `last_seen_at` is stale for 15 minutes.
12. - **Canonical pilot schema removed notification storage.** `database/schemas/shs_schema_v2.sql` drops `notifications` and `push_tokens`, and `database/README.md` says they are intentionally removed from the pilot schema.
13. - **Frontend has partial notification-era leftovers.** Shared API/types still define `notificationAPI`, `pushTokenAPI`, and `SignNotification`, but the mobile app currently uses device polling plus a `NotificationDetailScreen` for viewing a `DeviceEvent`, not an inbox. `expo-notifications` appears in `package-lock.json` but is not declared in `apps/mobile/package.json`.
14. 
15. ## Recommended Direction
16. 
17. Build this in two layers so the pilot can ship incrementally:
18. 
19. 1. **Backend-authored notification records** for `assistance_requested` and `offline`, with deduplication and read state.
20. 2. **Mobile consumption path** that can start as an in-app inbox/polling experience, with **Expo push delivery added only if required**.
21. 
22. This keeps the first vertical slice aligned with the pilot guidance in `PILOT.md`, which explicitly allows polling as the notification path.
23. 
24. ## Architecture Decisions
25. 
26. - **Treat notifications as a backend concern.** The backend should decide when a notification-worthy event occurs and persist a notification record instead of asking the mobile app to infer it.
27. - **Move offline detection server-side.** A real offline notification requires a server-side stale-device evaluator because the current frontend-only stale logic cannot notify a user who is not actively looking at the app.
28. - **Reuse device events as the source of truth.** Notification generation should hang off device status transitions / stale detection so the system has one auditable event stream.
29. - **Keep push optional.** Implement the persistence + API contract first; make Expo push an add-on delivery path.
30. 
31. ## Task List
32.

34.

36. 
37. **Description:** Decide the operator experience and backend rules before coding: notification channels, recipients, offline threshold, duplicate suppression, and how notifications relate to the existing pilot event history.
38. 
39. **Acceptance criteria:**
40. - A single source of truth exists for which events create notifications (`assistance_requested`, `offline`).
41. - The plan defines the recipient model for pilot users.
42. - The plan defines whether the first implementation is inbox-only, push-enabled, or both.
43. 
44. **Verification:**
45. - Open questions are resolved and captured in the implementation notes.

248. ## Risks and Mitigations
249. 
250. | Risk | Impact | Mitigation |
251. |---|---|---|
252. | Offline is only client-derived today, so notifications would be inconsistent if server logic is not added | High | Introduce a backend stale-device evaluator and make backend state authoritative |
253. | Reintroducing notifications may conflict with the pilot schema simplification | Medium | Keep the schema minimal and tied only to pilot events, not the old multi-org notification model |
254. | Push implementation could add native/app complexity without pilot value | Medium | Ship inbox/polling first and gate push behind an explicit scope decision |
255. | Duplicate notifications from repeated wave detections or repeated offline sweeps | High | Add idempotency rules keyed by unresolved request/offline incident |

✔ #63 view - view the file at C:\Users\KBishop\.copilot\session-state\f991aa83-a4fc-40b6-9eaa-ef50b1fb8920\plan.md. 7m 48s
C:\Users\KBishop\.copilot\session-state\f991aa83-a4fc-40b6-9eaa-ef50b1fb8920\plan.md (lines 1-260)
1. # Implementation Plan: Sign Offline / Assistance Notifications
2. 
3. ## Problem
4. 
5. Add operator notifications when a sign enters `assistance_requested`, without breaking the current one-sign pilot flow. `Offline` will stay out of scope for this plan.
6. 
7. ## Current State Summary
8. 
9. - **Backend runtime is pilot-only.** `backend/app/main.py` mounts only auth, inference, and device routes. Notification and push-token endpoints are currently absent, and `backend/tests/test_removed_routes.py` asserts `/api/v1/notifications` and `/api/v1/push-tokens` return 404.
10. - **Assistance requests already exist as device events.** `backend/app/routes/inference.py` changes a device from `available` to `assistance_requested` and records a `device_events` row via `device_service.transition_device_status(...)`.
11. - **Offline is only a frontend interpretation today.** The backend updates `devices.last_seen_at`, but it never transitions a device to `offline` or emits an offline event. `frontend_new/apps/mobile/src/screens/pilotStatus.ts` derives `offline` locally when `last_seen_at` is stale for 15 minutes. This stays as-is for now.
12. - **Canonical pilot schema removed notification storage.** `database/schemas/shs_schema_v2.sql` drops `notifications` and `push_tokens`, and `database/README.md` says they are intentionally removed from the pilot schema.
13. - **Frontend has partial notification-era leftovers.** Shared API/types still define `notificationAPI`, `pushTokenAPI`, and `SignNotification`, but the mobile app currently uses device polling plus a `NotificationDetailScreen` for viewing a `DeviceEvent`, not an inbox. `expo-notifications` appears in `package-lock.json` but is not declared in `apps/mobile/package.json`.
14. 
15. ## Recommended Direction
16. 
17. Build this in two layers, with push included in the initial release:
18. 
19. 1. **Backend-authored notification records** for `assistance_requested`, with deduplication and read state.
20. 2. **Mobile consumption path** with an in-app inbox plus **Expo push delivery** for operators, while keeping stored notifications as the source of truth.
21. 
22. This still fits the pilot because the inbox/polling flow remains authoritative; push becomes an additional delivery channel rather than the only way to discover an alert.
23. 
24. ## Scope Decisions Captured
25. 
26. - **Delivery mode:** in-app notifications **and** push notifications in the first release
27. - **Audience:** all operators receive notifications by default, with an **opt-out** control
28. - **Notification event:** only `assistance_requested` is in scope
29. - **Deferred:** backend-authored `offline` incidents and offline notifications
30. 
31. ## Architecture Decisions
32. 
33. - **Treat notifications as a backend concern.** The backend should decide when a notification-worthy event occurs and persist a notification record instead of asking the mobile app to infer it.
34. - **Reuse device events as the source of truth.** Notification generation should hang off the existing assistance-request status transition so the system has one auditable event stream.
35. - **Keep persisted notifications canonical even with push enabled.** Push should mirror a saved notification record, not replace it.
36. - **Default to notify-all with opt-out.** The simplest pilot model is "all authenticated operators are subscribed unless they disable notifications."
37. - **Defer server-side offline handling.** The existing client-side stale/offline display remains unchanged until offline notifications are explicitly brought into scope.
38. 
39. ## Task List
40. 
41. ### Phase 1: Define the contract and data model
42. 
43. #### Task 1: Finalize notification scope and delivery semantics
44. 
45. **Description:** Decide the operator experience and backend rules before coding: notification channels, recipients, duplicate suppression, opt-out behavior, and how notifications relate to the existing pilot event history.
46. 
47. **Acceptance criteria:**
48. - A single source of truth exists for which events create notifications (`assistance_requested` only in this phase).
49. - The plan defines the recipient model for pilot users.
50. - The plan defines whether the first implementation is inbox-only, push-enabled, or both.
51. 
52. **Verification:**
53. - Open questions are resolved and captured in the implementation notes.
54. 
55. **Dependencies:** None
56. 
57. **Files likely touched:**
58. - `C:\Users\KBishop\.copilot\session-state\f991aa83-a4fc-40b6-9eaa-ef50b1fb8920\plan.md`
59. - `README.md`
60. - `PILOT.md`
61. 
62. **Estimated scope:** Small
63. 
64. #### Task 2: Reintroduce notification persistence in the pilot schema
65. 
66. **Description:** Add the minimal database shape needed for notifications, including `notifications`, `push_tokens`, and a lightweight operator preference/opt-out mechanism. Keep the schema pilot-friendly and keyed off existing `users`, `devices`, and `device_events`.
67. 
68. **Acceptance criteria:**
69. - The schema can store a notification record tied to a triggering device event or device.
70. - Read/unread state is supported for the mobile app.
71. - Push tokens can be stored per user/device.
72. - Operators can opt out without deleting historical notification records.
73. 
74. **Verification:**
75. - `cd database && npm run migrate`
76. 
77. **Dependencies:** Task 1
78.

87. ### Checkpoint: Foundation

92. ### Phase 2: Backend event generation and APIs

95.

97.

100. - Repeated wave detections do not spam duplicate unread notifications for the same outstanding request.
101. - Existing device-event behavior remains intact.

📦 #79 task (Completed) 12m 2s
💬 #79 Copilot 14m 33s

Here is my critique across all four areas.

Critique: Schema/Contract Slice for Assistance-Request Notifications

Blocking Issues

1. device_event_id is nullable in the existing SignNotification type — making the DB column nullable destroys your deduplication anchor

auth.ts:62 defines device_event_id: string | null. If the schema mirrors this with a nullable column, there is no reliable way to enforce one notification per device_events row later. A UNIQUE(device_event_id) constraint cannot be applied to a nullable column without special handling (it allows multiple NULLs in standard SQL). The assistance-request trigger always produces a device_events row via transition_device_status (see device_service.py:163), so for this notification type there is no legitimate case for a null device_event_id. Define the column as NOT NULL with a FK to device_events(id) in the schema. Keep the frontend type nullable only for display cases where the event is unavailable (i.e. it's a type concern, not a schema concern). Without this, the dedup UNIQUE constraint you'll need later cannot be added cleanly.

2. Opt-out preference has no schema representation — the next slice will be forced to combine schema + service changes

The "default notify-all with opt-out" plan appears nowhere in the existing schema or types. If opt-out storage is deferred to the routes/service slice, that slice will need a schema migration AND service wiring simultaneously, coupling two concerns and negating the value of the schema-first approach. This decision needs to land now. The simplest option that avoids touching the existing users DDL is a separate notification_preferences(user_id UUID PK REFERENCES users(id), opted_out BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE, updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ) table. Adding it inline to users also works but forces a more disruptive schema file change. Either is fine — the risk is leaving it unresolved and letting the next slice guess.

Non-Blocking Issues

3. test_removed_routes.py will silently block CI in the routes slice unless explicitly flagged now

test_removed_routes.py:11-16 asserts GET /api/v1/notifications → 404 and GET /api/v1/push-tokens → 404. The test name ("test_non_pilot_routes_are_gone") reads as a permanent sentinel, so the developer picking up the routes slice may not think to touch it. When the routes are mounted, the suite breaks without a clear error message explaining why. Add a comment in test_removed_routes.py and/or the schema PILOT.md update explicitly stating: "the routes slice must remove the /notifications and /push-tokens entries from this test when mounting those routers." Without this, the next developer will hit a confusing, unexplained CI failure.

4. PILOT.md currently categorizes push notifications as a post-pilot item — updating it in this slice creates a live contradiction

PILOT.md:253 lists "Push notifications" under "Post-pilot items." If this slice edits PILOT.md to bring assistance-request push in-scope without reconciling that section, the document becomes self-contradictory. Any update to PILOT.md in this slice must simultaneously remove or qualify that post-pilot entry; otherwise the document is unreliable as a scope reference.

Suggestions

5. push_tokens table: decide and document its inclusion or deferral explicitly in this slice

The schema drops push_tokens and does not recreate it. Expo push requires token persistence. If push is in scope for the notification feature, push_tokens must be defined in this schema slice or the routes slice will have to make a schema change mid-implementation. If push token registration is still deferred (consistent with PILOT.md's current language), make that explicit in the schema comments and plan so the routes slice author doesn't have to make the call.

6. Notification creation atomicity with the transition transaction is an unresolved architectural contract

device_service.py:123-173 writes the status update and device_events row in a single async with conn.transaction() block. If notifications rows are to be created in the same transaction (safest — prevents missed notifications on partial failure), the schema and service contract for that insert location needs to be established now. If notifications are written as an async side-effect after the transaction (e.g., a background task or event bus), there is a window where the status changes but the notification is lost silently. This is an architectural contract that the schema slice is the right place to specify — documenting it as a comment in the schema or PILOT.md so the service slice doesn't make the wrong call.

C:\Users\KBishop\code\apps\smart-handicap-sign\PILOT.md (lines 15-45)
15. ## What the pilot should include
16. 
17. ### Core scope
18. 
19. - **One physical sign**
20. - **One backend environment**
21. - **One organization or one shared operator account**
22. - **One staff-facing mobile app flow**
23. - **One notification path**: app polling is acceptable; push notifications are optional
24. - **One install location**
25. - **Basic event history** for requests, acknowledgements, and resolutions
26. 
27. ### Required states
28. 
29. - `available`
30. - `assistance_requested`
31. - `assistance_in_progress`
32. - `offline`
33. - return to `available`
34. 
35. For pilot purposes, `offline` should mean the sign has missed its expected backend check-ins long enough that staff should not trust the displayed availability until the device reconnects.
36. 
37. ### Required working surfaces in this repo
38. 
39. - **Firmware/device loop**
40.   - Poll sign status
41.   - Sample and send wave data
42.   - Respect backend status before classifying
43. - **Backend**
44.   - `POST /api/v1/inference/classify`
45.   - `GET /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/status`
✔ #89 view - view the file at C:\Users\KBishop\code\apps\smart-handicap-sign\PILOT.md. 15m 22s
C:\Users\KBishop\code\apps\smart-handicap-sign\PILOT.md (lines 88-120)
88. ## What may need to be added or tightened before pilot launch
89. 
90. ### Product and UX
91. 
92. - A clearly named **pilot operator flow**:
93.   - see current sign status
94.   - see new request
95.   - acknowledge
96.   - resolve
97. - Clear copy for each status so staff can act without training
98. - A visible last-updated or last-seen timestamp for device freshness
99. - A simple error/offline indicator for the sign
100. 
101. ### Backend
102. 
103. - Confirm `assistance_requested -> assistance_in_progress -> available` is the only supported operator loop for pilot
104. - Define the freshness rule that moves a sign into `offline`
105. - Ensure acknowledge and resolve actions create auditable device events
106. - Ensure one wave does not create noisy duplicate requests while already in a requested/in-progress state
107. - Ensure device status polling remains lightweight and stable
108. - Ensure the pilot can run with seeded data and minimal setup steps
109. 
110. ### Frontend
111. 
112. - Make the home screen robust when exactly one device is present
113. - Show the most recent request clearly
114. - Show `offline` as a distinct state, not as generic failure text
115. - Prevent double taps on acknowledge / resolve actions
116. - Show actionable failure states if the backend call fails
117. - Keep navigation minimal for pilot users
118. 
119. ### Firmware / device setup
120.
✔ #90 view - view the file at C:\Users\KBishop\code\apps\smart-handicap-sign\PILOT.md. 15m 22s
C:\Users\KBishop\code\apps\smart-handicap-sign\PILOT.md (lines 150-210)
150.   - [ ] one organization or shared pilot account
151.   - [ ] one active device
152.   - [ ] one fixed site/parking-space assignment if needed
153. - [ ] Device serial number and auth token are confirmed
154. 
155. ### Device readiness
156. 
157. - [ ] Firmware is flashed on the pilot sign
158. - [ ] Sign can reach Wi-Fi reliably from the installation location
159. - [ ] Sign can reach backend endpoints reliably
160. - [ ] Sign status polling works
161. - [ ] Sign transitions to `offline` when expected connectivity is lost and recovers when connectivity returns
162. - [ ] Wave classification requests succeed
163. - [ ] LED/status indication is correct for each pilot state
164. 
165. ### App readiness
166. 
167. - [ ] Operator can log in
168. - [ ] Operator can view the pilot sign from the home screen
169. - [ ] Operator can acknowledge a request
170. - [ ] Operator can resolve a request
171. - [ ] Operator can recover from a transient backend failure without app restart
172. 
173. ### Operational readiness
174. 
175. - [ ] Staff know what to do when a request appears
176. - [ ] Staff know expected response-time target for the pilot
177. - [ ] A contact person is assigned for pilot issues
178. - [ ] A rollback/manual fallback exists if the sign or backend fails
179. 
180. ## Tests that should pass before pilot launch
181. 
182. ## 1. Backend API behavior
183. 
184. - [ ] `GET /health` returns healthy in the pilot environment
185. - [ ] `GET /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/status` returns the current device state for the pilot sign
186. - [ ] The backend marks the sign `offline` after the defined missed-check-in window
187. - [ ] `POST /api/v1/inference/classify` accepts valid 512-sample payloads from the pilot device
188. - [ ] A positive classification changes the sign to `assistance_requested`
189. - [ ] A positive classification creates a device event
190. - [ ] `POST /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/acknowledge` changes state to `assistance_in_progress`
191. - [ ] `POST /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/resolve` changes state back to `available`
192. - [ ] Invalid or unauthorized device submissions are rejected
193. - [ ] Repeated classifications do not create invalid state transitions or unbounded duplicate alerts
194. 
195. ## 2. Frontend operator workflow
196. 
197. - [ ] Operator login succeeds
198. - [ ] Home screen loads with the pilot sign visible
199. - [ ] Sign status updates are visible without confusing navigation
200. - [ ] `offline` is clearly distinguishable from `available` and request states
201. - [ ] A newly requested assistance event becomes visible to staff quickly enough for the pilot
202. - [ ] Acknowledge action updates UI and backend state correctly
203. - [ ] Resolve action updates UI and backend state correctly
204. - [ ] App handles temporary API failures with a clear retry path
205. 
206. ## 3. Device and firmware behavior
207. 
208. - [ ] Device authenticates successfully with backend
209. - [ ] Device polls status successfully on boot
210. - [ ] Device only submits classify requests when status is `available`

C:\Users\KBishop\code\apps\smart-handicap-sign\PILOT.md (lines 226-260)
226. ## 5. Negative and recovery scenarios
227. 
228. - [ ] Non-wave/noise does not frequently trigger false requests during a short observation run
229. - [ ] If the backend is down, the device fails safely
230. - [ ] If the app is unavailable, the request still exists in backend state/event history
231. - [ ] If a request is already active, additional detections do not break the workflow
232. - [ ] If the device stops checking in, the sign becomes `offline` within the expected window
233. - [ ] If the device reconnects after being offline, it returns to the correct backend-driven state
234. - [ ] If the sign reboots, it returns to the correct backend-driven state
235. 
236. ## Suggested pilot exit criteria
237. 
238. The pilot is ready to launch when all of the following are true:
239. 
240. - [ ] The one-sign assistance loop works end to end
241. - [ ] Staff can operate the system without developer intervention
242. - [ ] The device remains connected and usable in the real install location
243. - [ ] Failures are understandable and recoverable
244. - [ ] Deferred features are no longer blocking decisions for launch
245. 
246. ## Post-pilot items
247. 
248. These should be evaluated **after** the pilot proves the core workflow:
249. 
250. - Push notifications
251. - Multi-sign dashboards
252. - Full installer claim flow
253. - Rich org/member/site administration
254. - OTA updates
255. - Better analytics and reporting
256. - Training-mode productization
257. - Production hardening for scale
258.

C:\Users\KBishop\code\apps\smart-handicap-sign\database\README.md (lines 1-220)
1. # Database
2. 
3. PostgreSQL 15 schema assets for the one-sign Hazard Hero pilot.
4. 
5. ## Canonical assets
6. 
7. - `schemas/shs_schema.sql` — bootstrap entrypoint used by Docker and local setup
8. - `schemas/shs_schema_v2.sql` — canonical pilot schema loaded by `shs_schema.sql`
9. - `seeds/dev_data_v2.sql` — deterministic pilot sign bootstrap data
10. - `scripts/migrate_v2.ts` — default migration entrypoint
11. 
12. ## Commands
13. 
14. Run these from `database/`:
15. 
16. ```bash
17. npm run migrate
18. npm run migrate:last-seen
19. npm run load:sign
20. npm run seed
21. ```
22. 
23. The scripts load `../backend/.env` and expect `POSTGRES_CONNECTION_STRING` (or `DATABASE_URL` for the sign load script) to point at the target PostgreSQL instance.
24. 
25. ## Migration behavior
26. 
27. `npm run migrate` drops and recreates the database as the pilot schema. It is destructive by design and should only be used where data reset is acceptable.
28. 
29. `npm run migrate:last-seen` is an additive migration that only ensures `devices.last_seen_at` exists on an already-provisioned pilot database.
30. 
31. ## Pilot schema overview
32. 
33. The pilot database keeps only the tables needed for a single operator + single sign workflow:
34. 
35. - `users`
36. - `profiles`
37. - `devices`
38. - `device_events`
39. - `notifications`
40. - `notification_preferences`
41. - `push_tokens`
42. 
43. ## Device states
44. 
45. `device_operational_status` supports only the pilot loop and basic health states:
46. 
47. - `available`
48. - `assistance_requested`
49. - `assistance_in_progress`
50. - `offline`
51. - `error`
52. 
53. Training states, organization tables, installation/claim workflow tables, and billing/subscription fields are intentionally removed from the canonical schema. The pilot notification schema only supports assistance-request alerts plus operator opt-out and Expo push token storage.
54. 
55. ## Assistance-request notifications
56. 
57. The pilot schema now includes the minimum persistence needed for operator notifications:
58. 
59. - `notifications` stores one assistance-request alert per `(user_id, device_event_id)` so later service code can suppress duplicates per operator.
60. - `notification_preferences` stores operator opt-out state. Missing rows should be treated as the pilot default: notifications enabled and push enabled.
61. - `push_tokens` stores Expo push tokens for authenticated operators.
62. 
63. `offline` remains a frontend-only stale indicator for now. The canonical schema does not create backend-authored offline incidents or offline notifications in this phase.
64. 
65. ## Pilot sign bootstrap
66. 
67. `npm run load:sign` applies `seeds/dev_data_v2.sql`, which creates only the pilot sign/device row required by the runtime API. It does not create user, profile, organization, parking-space, or device-event records.
68. 
69. `npm run seed` is kept as a backwards-compatible alias for the same sign-only load.
70. 
71. The seeded device token is `pilot-device-token` with serial `SHS-2605-S01-A7K-00001-J` for local pilot testing.
72.
✔ #97 view - view the file at C:\Users\KBishop\code\apps\smart-handicap-sign\PILOT.md. 16m 10s
C:\Users\KBishop\code\apps\smart-handicap-sign\PILOT.md (lines 15-260)
15. ## What the pilot should include
16. 
17. ### Core scope
18. 
19. - **One physical sign**
20. - **One backend environment**
21. - **One organization or one shared operator account**
22. - **One staff-facing mobile app flow**
23. - **One notification path**: assistance-request notifications should exist in-app and may also be delivered by push; `offline` remains a frontend-only stale indicator for now
24. - **One install location**
25. - **Basic event history** for requests, acknowledgements, and resolutions
26. 
27. ### Required states
28. 
29. - `available`
30. - `assistance_requested`
31. - `assistance_in_progress`
32. - `offline`
33. - return to `available`
34. 
35. For pilot purposes, `offline` should mean the sign has missed its expected backend check-ins long enough that staff should not trust the displayed availability until the device reconnects.
36. 
37. ### Required working surfaces in this repo
38. 
39. - **Firmware/device loop**
40.   - Poll sign status
41.   - Sample and send wave data
42.   - Respect backend status before classifying
43. - **Backend**
44.   - `POST /api/v1/inference/classify`
45.   - `GET /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/status`
46.   - `POST /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/acknowledge`
47.   - `POST /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/resolve`
48.   - device event logging
49. - **Frontend**
50.   - Login
51.   - Home screen showing current sign status
52.   - Acknowledge action
53.   - Resolve action
54.   - Basic request/event visibility
55. 
56. ## What should be removed from pilot scope
57. 
58. These items may remain in the repo, but they should be treated as **out of scope for pilot launch** and not block pilot completion.
59. 
60. ### Defer from launch
61. 
62. - Multi-organization administration
63. - Full member management and role complexity beyond what one pilot operator needs
64. - Full QR claim/install workflow
65. - Site and parking-space management UI beyond one seeded assignment
66. - Device fleet management for many devices
67. - Transfer / revoke / release workflows for pilot operations
68. - Claim ID regeneration workflows
69. - Push-token registration as a launch dependency
70. - Inference debug screens as part of the operator workflow
71. - OTA update workflows as a launch dependency
72. - Advanced firmware provisioning flows unless needed for this one install
73. - Training states:
74.   - `training_ready`
75.   - `training_positive`
76.   - `training_negative`
77. - Billing / subscription concepts
78. - Any old social/media/template leftovers in documentation
79. 
80. ### Recommended repo-level simplifications for pilot focus
81. 
82. - **Hide or ignore** non-pilot screens from normal navigation if they distract from the operator flow.
83. - **Seed one known device** and one known user instead of requiring the full installer claim process.
84. - **Treat sites / parking spaces as fixed setup data** for the pilot, not operator-managed content.
85. - **Use polling first**; add push later only if polling is too slow.
86. - **Make the home screen the primary pilot surface** and avoid requiring operators to visit secondary admin screens.
87. 
88. ## What may need to be added or tightened before pilot launch
89. 
90. ### Product and UX
91. 
92. - A clearly named **pilot operator flow**:
93.   - see current sign status
94.   - see new request
95.   - acknowledge
96.   - resolve
97. - Clear copy for each status so staff can act without training
98. - A visible last-updated or last-seen timestamp for device freshness
99. - A simple error/offline indicator for the sign
100. 
101. ### Backend
102. 
103. - Confirm `assistance_requested -> assistance_in_progress -> available` is the only supported operator loop for pilot
104. - Keep the current frontend-only stale/offline indicator clear for operators without making backend offline handling a launch dependency
105. - Add assistance-request notifications without changing the core sign state machine
106. - Ensure acknowledge and resolve actions create auditable device events
107. - Ensure one wave does not create noisy duplicate requests while already in a requested/in-progress state
108. - Ensure device status polling remains lightweight and stable
109. - Ensure the pilot can run with seeded data and minimal setup steps
110. 
111. ### Frontend
112. 
113. - Make the home screen robust when exactly one device is present
114. - Show the most recent request clearly
115. - Show `offline` as a distinct state, not as generic failure text
116. - Prevent double taps on acknowledge / resolve actions
117. - Show actionable failure states if the backend call fails
118. - Keep navigation minimal for pilot users
119. 
120. ### Firmware / device setup
121. 
122. - Lock in the production-like URL and credentials for the pilot device
123. - Verify the sign behaves safely when backend is unreachable
124. - Verify LED/status behavior matches the backend state machine
125. - Verify the sign does not continuously spam classify requests when unavailable
126. 
127. ### Documentation and ops
128. 
129. - Update repo-facing docs so the pilot story is obvious
130. - Document exact install steps for the one pilot sign
131. - Document operator steps for handling a request
132. - Document recovery steps for:
133.   - sign offline
134.   - backend unavailable
135.   - sign stuck in requested/in-progress state
136. 
137. ## Pilot launch checklist
138. 
139. ### Scope freeze
140. 
141. - [ ] Pilot success criteria are limited to one-sign end-to-end assistance handling
142. - [ ] Non-pilot features are explicitly marked as deferred
143. - [ ] Operators know which app screens are in scope for launch
144. 
145. ### Environment and data
146. 
147. - [ ] Backend environment is deployed and reachable from the sign
148. - [ ] Database schema is applied
149. - [ ] Seed data or manual setup creates:
150.   - [ ] one operator user
151.   - [ ] one organization or shared pilot account
152.   - [ ] one active device
153.   - [ ] one fixed site/parking-space assignment if needed
154. - [ ] Device serial number and auth token are confirmed
155. 
156. ### Device readiness
157. 
158. - [ ] Firmware is flashed on the pilot sign
159. - [ ] Sign can reach Wi-Fi reliably from the installation location
160. - [ ] Sign can reach backend endpoints reliably
161. - [ ] Sign status polling works
162. - [ ] If the sign stops checking in, the app still shows the existing stale/offline indicator clearly enough for pilot operators
163. - [ ] Wave classification requests succeed
164. - [ ] LED/status indication is correct for each pilot state
165. 
166. ### App readiness
167. 
168. - [ ] Operator can log in
169. - [ ] Operator can view the pilot sign from the home screen
170. - [ ] Operator can acknowledge a request
171. - [ ] Operator can resolve a request
172. - [ ] Operator can recover from a transient backend failure without app restart
173. 
174. ### Operational readiness
175. 
176. - [ ] Staff know what to do when a request appears
177. - [ ] Staff know expected response-time target for the pilot
178. - [ ] A contact person is assigned for pilot issues
179. - [ ] A rollback/manual fallback exists if the sign or backend fails
180. 
181. ## Tests that should pass before pilot launch
182. 
183. ## 1. Backend API behavior
184. 
185. - [ ] `GET /health` returns healthy in the pilot environment
186. - [ ] `GET /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/status` returns the current device state for the pilot sign
187. - [ ] `POST /api/v1/inference/classify` accepts valid 512-sample payloads from the pilot device
188. - [ ] A positive classification changes the sign to `assistance_requested`
189. - [ ] A positive classification creates a device event
190. - [ ] A positive classification creates one assistance-request notification per opted-in operator
191. - [ ] `POST /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/acknowledge` changes state to `assistance_in_progress`
192. - [ ] `POST /api/v1/devices/{serial_number}/resolve` changes state back to `available`
193. - [ ] Invalid or unauthorized device submissions are rejected
194. - [ ] Repeated classifications do not create invalid state transitions or unbounded duplicate alerts
195. 
196. ## 2. Frontend operator workflow
197. 
198. - [ ] Operator login succeeds
199. - [ ] Home screen loads with the pilot sign visible
200. - [ ] Sign status updates are visible without confusing navigation
201. - [ ] `offline` is clearly distinguishable from `available` and request states
202. - [ ] A newly requested assistance event becomes visible to staff quickly enough for the pilot
203. - [ ] Assistance-request notifications can be opened, read, and opted out of by an operator
204. - [ ] Acknowledge action updates UI and backend state correctly
205. - [ ] Resolve action updates UI and backend state correctly
206. - [ ] App handles temporary API failures with a clear retry path
207. 
208. ## 3. Device and firmware behavior
209. 
210. - [ ] Device authenticates successfully with backend
211. - [ ] Device polls status successfully on boot
212. - [ ] Device only submits classify requests when status is `available`
213. - [ ] Device remains stable during repeated polling/classification cycles
214. - [ ] Device recovers cleanly from temporary Wi-Fi loss
215. - [ ] Device does not enter a broken loop after backend errors
216. 
217. ## 4. End-to-end pilot scenario
218. 
219. - [ ] Starting state is `available`
220. - [ ] A real user wave at the installed sign generates `assistance_requested`
221. - [ ] Staff sees the request on the app
222. - [ ] Staff acknowledges the request
223. - [ ] Sign becomes `assistance_in_progress`
224. - [ ] Staff resolves the request
225. - [ ] Sign returns to `available`
226. - [ ] Event history shows the full sequence with timestamps
227. 
228. ## 5. Negative and recovery scenarios
229. 
230. - [ ] Non-wave/noise does not frequently trigger false requests during a short observation run
231. - [ ] If the backend is down, the device fails safely
232. - [ ] If the app is unavailable, the request still exists in backend state/event history
233. - [ ] If a request is already active, additional detections do not break the workflow
234. - [ ] If the device stops checking in, operators still see the existing stale/offline indicator in the app
235. - [ ] If the sign reboots, it returns to the correct backend-driven state
236. 
237. ## Suggested pilot exit criteria
238. 
239. The pilot is ready to launch when all of the following are true:
240. 
241. - [ ] The one-sign assistance loop works end to end
242. - [ ] Staff can operate the system without developer intervention
243. - [ ] The device remains connected and usable in the real install location
244. - [ ] Failures are understandable and recoverable
245. - [ ] Deferred features are no longer blocking decisions for launch
246. 
247. ## Post-pilot items
248. 
249. These should be evaluated **after** the pilot proves the core workflow:
250. 
251. - Multi-sign dashboards
252. - Full installer claim flow
253. - Rich org/member/site administration
254. - OTA updates
255. - Better analytics and reporting
256. - Training-mode productization
257. - Production hardening for scale
258.

+## Assistance-request notifications
+

+
